            "Yes. And you’re right to want this **as a production beat map** (not prose), but still **Te’Oga-safe** and consistent with the **locked bible** (POVs, Soulpulse counts, knowledge gates, no early sex, etc.).\n\n**Constraints I will follow in this beat map:** Te’Oga lexicon (Tide/Anneal/Span/Bar/Cable; Upslope/Downslope; Stone/Load), **no Earth units/directions**, no future-leaking past N01, and I’ll keep the beats aligned to the locked chapter assignments (Ch3 = Jhace only; Ch5 = Tiffani, etc.). I’ll also avoid “like/as if” phrasing here so the document stays stylistically clean.\n\n---\n\n# N01: THE GRIP THAT HOLDS — COMPLETE BEAT MAP (Ch 1–12)\n*Interludes + Epilogue remain placeholders per your instruction.*\n\n## CHAPTER 1 — Something Wrong\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 0, Kindling | **Beat:** Observation | **Soulpulse:** 0  \n1) Junction Seven memorial plaque; Jhace reads all names; body goes tight; he logs anyway.  \n2) Inspector kit check: slate, chalk, cord, collar keys, wedge slips, lamp oil.  \n3) Palm-to-pipe check: baseline grid-hum present; doubled harmonic present.  \n4) Dust drop in a narrow strip; repeats in timed pulses; he counts by breath and logs interval.  \n5) He repeats the check at Junction Nine; same doubled harmonic; not local.  \n6) Control check at a side spur: baseline changes with flow; doubled harmonic persists.  \n7) Junction Twelve: guild crew mid-argument; they want flow maintained.  \n8) Jhace inspects collar seam bead, torque bias, sealant expression; logs “shift under load.”  \n9) He orders isolation; resistance escalates; he cites Junction Seven dead without raising voice.  \n10) Valve turns; baseline hum dips; doubled harmonic persists; he logs the persistence as key proof.  \n11) Micro-shudder underfoot; lamps twitch; weight reduces briefly, then returns harshly; no one has language yet.  \n12) Jhace refuses desk escalation; follows harmonic deeper; chooses action over protocol.  \n13) He checks stone itself, not pipe; pulse repeats through wall contact.  \n14) He marks route to Sector Fourteen on slate map; writes “pressure under foundation.”  \n15) He gives the crew a contingency: hold isolation; send runner to Bram if he doesn’t return.  \n16) He moves deeper with measured pace; no running; breath controlled; focus narrowed.  \n17) Closing image: palm on stone, doubled harmonic stronger; he logs “off-local, escalating.”\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 2 — Glass That Listens\n**POV:** Tiffani | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 0, Pouring | **Beat:** Observation | **Soulpulse:** 0  \n1) Observatory platform routine: theodolite setup, lens plate check, clamp torque, base grit sweep.  \n2) Seven-Three read: offset beyond tolerance; she resets; repeats; offset persists.  \n3) Control star read: stable; her instrument is not the source.  \n4) Glass plate bins begin a low resonance; pitch climbs into teeth; she logs “resonance without wind source.”  \n5) Pella arrives with bread and chatter; Tiffani cuts it down; keeps the read cycle intact.  \n6) Grid-hum phase shift: whine then low baseline; theodolite read steps, not drifts; she logs discrete steps.  \n7) Metallic taste arrives before visible dust; she checks slate seams; finds copper-gold particulate collecting.  \n8) She draws projection curve; it breaks into segments; she writes “external forcing.”  \n9) Warning bell protocol: she pulls the cord with sequence; bell tone rings flat then corrects.  \n10) Shock arrives through structure; instrument feet scrape; page lifts and slaps back down; she pins logbook by reflex.  \n11) Dust column rises beyond roofline; ejection is fast and vertical; debris arcs widen.  \n12) Gravity reduction interval: boots lose full pressure; stomach lifts; she counts heartbeats.  \n13) Gravity returns harshly; platform rail takes impact through wrists; she tastes blood at gumline.  \n14) She sights through dust: spindle visible as dark absence; optical distortion tracks its boundary; she logs “bent-light.”  \n15) Dust fall begins steady; copper-gold particulate sticks to lashes and lip seams.  \n16) Tiffani pivots from observation to field response: kit list out loud; Pella repeats it back.  \n17) She bans the lift; chooses stairs due to grid instability; closes chapter moving Downslope.\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 3 — The Piercing\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 0, Shaping/Striking | **Beat:** Crisis | **Soulpulse:** 2 uses  \n1) Jhace comes up from Underface into street fracture: leaning walls, dust curtains, wrong grid-hum.  \n2) Copper-gold dust taste hits immediately; it sticks to sweat seams on neck and knuckles.  \n3) Gravity reduction interval begins; loose objects lift; he counts heartbeats without deciding to.  \n4) Gravity returns harshly; knees buckle; a nearby signpost snaps at base.  \n5) Eruption column visible in distance; pressure wall arrives before the roar; ribs vibrate; breath interrupts.  \n6) Market corridor: roof beam drops; Chloen pinned; leg crushed; people freeze.  \n7) Jhace tries brute lift; load does not move; aftershock threat continues; he chooses contact hold.  \n8) **Soulpulse Use #1 activation:** palms flat to timber; intent is protective; panic is present; copper-gold glow enters grain.  \n9) Timber response: hold stabilizes; beam stops settling; evac hands pull Chloen free.  \n10) **Aftermath cost:** tremor begins in fingers; spreads to wrists; he cannot stop it with grip.  \n11) Secondary crisis: doorway post failing; people trapped under lintel; time pressure spikes.  \n12) **Soulpulse Use #2 activation:** palms to post; hold for evacuation; glow threads along crack paths.  \n13) Evac completes; he releases; post settles into a worse lean but does not collapse immediately.  \n14) **Aftermath cost escalates:** forearm pain, tremor amplitude increases; mouth tastes copper and iron.  \n15) Tiffani arrives with logbook and no awe; she demands data; he refuses name.  \n16) She marks the post with chalk; orders bracing; he watches her read load paths fast.  \n17) Closing: they move toward the next failure site in parallel without agreeing to.\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 4 — After the Shudder\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 1, Kindling | **Beat:** Trial/Failure | **Soulpulse:** 2 uses (1 failed, 1 success)  \n1) Bram’s workshop becomes staging: slates, wedges, nails, triage lists; dust coats everything.  \n2) Jhace wakes with tremor at rest; can’t set a nail clean; shame lands as heat in face.  \n3) He attempts a simple repair anyway; misses strikes; stops before he injures someone.  \n4) Tiffani appears to observe; she does not comfort; she asks for repeatable measures.  \n5) He tests non-emergency activation on a hairline crack.  \n6) **Soulpulse Use #3 fails:** no glow, no response; only tremor spike from effort and frustration.  \n7) Tiffani writes: “no imminent failure; intent not matched to need; response absent.”  \n8) Runner arrives: brace shifted at kiln corridor during aftershock; people trapped by sagging span.  \n9) They move; Tiffani marks three load points with chalk; she bans crowd weight near the failing edge.  \n10) Jhace braces conventionally first: wedges, cord tension, temporary posts; buys seconds.  \n11) Aftershock hits; conventional brace begins to slip; critical threat becomes immediate.  \n12) **Soulpulse Use #4 activation:** contact + protective need; glow threads into brace interface.  \n13) Structure holds long enough for evacuation; he releases on her command.  \n14) **Cost:** tremor persists; vein-lines appear briefly during use; exhaustion hits after release.  \n15) Kylar appears with tremor and fear; he tries to hide hands; Jhace sees it anyway.  \n16) Tiffani frames training: “learning where to press when the response occurs.”  \n17) Closing: Jhace agrees to be measured, not because he likes it, because the math is real.\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 5 — Where to Press\n**POV:** Tiffani | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 1, Pouring | **Beat:** Training/Method | **Soulpulse:** 0  \n1) Tiffani salvages what she can: bent theodolite parts, cracked plates, intact logbook; grief stays under procedure.  \n2) She sets a measurement station in Bram’s space: slate grid, chalk marks, tremor sampling at rest and post-exertion.  \n3) She catalogs Jhace’s four events so far: two activations, one failure, one success; writes activation condition in plain terms.  \n4) She draws cost curve; projects escalation; tells him his hands will become unusable without limits.  \n5) Jhace pushes back: people are dying; he refuses delay; he tries to turn it into morality.  \n6) Tiffani refuses the frame; she translates morality into logistics: dead operator saves no one.  \n7) Bram sets boundary: workshop access conditional; no uncontrolled activations inside.  \n8) They agree to method: her marks, his execution, her stop command.  \n9) She develops “contact point selection” as primary control lever; not “more power.”  \n10) She designs a field checklist: assess load, brace conventionally, set timer, activate only if imminent.  \n11) Pella forces food into her hands; Tiffani accepts without apology; the hunger is now a variable she manages.  \n12) Tiffani notes her own micro-tremor from exhaustion; she logs it but does not dramatize it.  \n13) Closing: a new slate arrives with a keystone risk; she packs chalk, cord, spare slate; she goes.\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 6 — The Arch Under Strain\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 1, Shaping/Striking | **Beat:** Crisis | **Soulpulse:** 1 use  \n1) Approach to the arch: crowd pressure, trapped households, aftershock timing fear in faces.  \n2) Tiffani clears space; orders bodies out of the load path; marks unsafe standing zones with chalk.  \n3) She inspects the keystone seat; identifies slip direction; marks three contact points on stone.  \n4) Jhace wants to palm the whole span; she blocks him physically; forces focus on the marks.  \n5) Conventional bracing goes in first: wedges, posts, cord tension; it reduces movement but does not stop it.  \n6) Aftershock begins; keystone creeps; dust bursts from mortar seams; sound changes in the arch throat.  \n7) **Soulpulse Use #5 activation:** Jhace contacts marked points; intent is “hold for evacuation,” not “save the arch forever.”  \n8) Copper-gold threads trace predicted load paths; Tiffani watches her marks light in sequence; she logs it later.  \n9) Evac moves; bodies clear; the arch holds through the peak.  \n10) Tiffani calls release at threshold; Jhace tries to hold longer; she repeats command with force.  \n11) He releases; tremor spreads into shoulders; vein-lines visible; exhaustion hits as a drop in motor control.  \n12) He collapses; Tiffani catches him; she shifts his weight to keep his head from striking stone.  \n13) Bram arrives with water and cloth; he uses humor to lower panic; he does not soften the truth.  \n14) Closing: Jhace accepts her authority in crisis; physical trust becomes a fact, not a promise.\n\n---\n\n## INTERLUDE I — The Watcher’s Ledger\n**Placeholder kept** (Corlexi POV, command-center slate chaos, registration language seed, no god reveal).\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 7 — Method\n**POV:** Tiffani | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 1, Quench | **Beat:** Recalibration/Debate | **Soulpulse:** 0  \n1) Tiffani designs a practice rig from salvage: stable posts, controlled load, marked stress lines.  \n2) Bram complains about wasted material; still helps; his boundary stays intact.  \n3) Jhace resents “training”; he wants field work; tremor makes him drop small tools; anger follows.  \n4) Tiffani reframes: efficiency reduces cost; cost reduction increases field capacity.  \n5) She tests narrowing: smaller contact area, shorter duration, pre-brace before activation.  \n6) Jhace follows instructions; cost reduction shows in tremor amplitude and recovery time.  \n7) She logs efficiency markers: glow intensity, vein-line duration, post-release tremor ramp.  \n8) Kylar pushes for access; Jhace refuses; fear hides under authority tone.  \n9) Tiffani corrects the language: not “ready,” but “safe.”  \n10) Debate: how to bring more manifesters in without creating casualties.  \n11) They draft safety protocol slates: consent, spotter, timer, rest, no unsupervised attempts.  \n12) Bram lands one cutting line that exposes their shared control issues; they both react; tension rises, then becomes focus.  \n13) Closing: a runner arrives with RRO note delivery; institutional pressure enters the room.\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 8 — What Breaks When You Push\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 2, Kindling | **Beat:** Trial/Failure | **Soulpulse:** 1 use  \n1) Kylar asks again; hands shaking; he wants certainty; Jhace offers delay; Tiffani offers controlled practice.  \n2) Their disagreement becomes personal: Jhace fears harm, Tiffani fears stagnation; neither says the fear cleanly.  \n3) Kylar leaves with unsaid anger; Jhace watches him go; does not chase immediately.  \n4) Collapse report: a cracked wall in a narrow lane; Kylar is there ahead of them.  \n5) Kylar attempts unsupervised activation; contact is full palm; intent floods; he cannot modulate.  \n6) Glow spikes; fracture lines light; the structure does not stabilize; it breaks into a sudden shear.  \n7) Stone fragments cut; people scream; Salee’s network arrives fast and extracts bodies.  \n8) Kylar seizes; vein-lines burn bright; tremor becomes violent; he cannot unclench.  \n9) Jhace and Tiffani hit triage mode: clear lane, stop bleed, stabilize airway, keep him alive.  \n10) Aftermath blame: Jhace blames delay; Tiffani blames pressure; both are partly right; neither gets relief.  \n11) Back at rig: they test refined technique under strict control to confirm cost reduction still holds.  \n12) **Soulpulse Use #6 activation (efficiency test):** controlled hold on rig; reduced cost confirmed; still present.  \n13) Closing: they write new rule in protocol slate: “No solo activation. Ever.”\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 9 — Asking\n**POV:** Tiffani | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 2, Pouring | **Beat:** Crisis/Synthesis | **Soulpulse:** 1 use (near Stage 2 boundary)  \n1) Kylar wakes; hands still tremor; shame blocks speech; Tiffani sits where he can see her slate.  \n2) Jhace asks the question directly: “What do you need.” No lecture. No rescue speech.  \n3) Kylar answers: he needs confidence under control, not speed; he needs a way to stop.  \n4) Tiffani redesigns method around tolerance: personal thresholds, stop signals, post-use care plan.  \n5) Jhace admits delay was fear; Tiffani admits push was control; they both correct course.  \n6) Major aftershock hits mid-conversation; dust lifts from beams; a support begins to walk.  \n7) Field response: failing support with people under it; Salee’s runners clear bodies with practiced routes.  \n8) **Soulpulse Use #7 activation:** extended duration hold; Jhace goes past safe time because he feels the load shift again.  \n9) Tiffani commands release; voice turns hard; she uses his name; she counts down heartbeats.  \n10) He releases late; vein-lines persist after; tremor remains high; he cannot stop shaking even at rest.  \n11) Tiffani documents the boundary symptoms without calling it “Stage 2” in-world: persistent vein glow, delayed motor recovery, breath disruption.  \n12) RRO summons arrives via Harlen; timing is bad; it reads as control move.  \n13) Closing: Tiffani and Jhace decide to align with need and networks, not committee timing.\n\n---\n\n## INTERLUDE II — Tides and Clarity\n**Placeholder kept** (Mobel harbor work, embedded shard, current shift, Salee network vs RRO bottleneck contrast, no god reveal).\n\n---\n\n## CHAPTER 10 — Integration\n**POV:** Jhace | **Tide/Phase:** Tide 2, Shaping | **Beat:** Recovery/Intimacy | **Soulpulse:** 0  \n1) Controlled site: damaged warehouse marked for demolition; no trapped bodies; time exists.  \n2) Tiffani runs full assessment: measure deflection, mark load paths, identify brace points.  \n3) Jhace executes conventional stabilization: wedges, posts, cord tension; they stand close without touching.  \n6) Tiffani states the achievement plainly: “We did not burn you.”  \n7) Jhace answers plainly: “We did it together.”  \n8) Salee arrives with an offer: mutual aid coordination;             "I understand. You want a comprehensive beat map for all 12 main chapters with the same granular detail I demonstrated for Chapter 1. The interludes and epilogue can remain as placeholder sections for now.\n\nLet me build this systematically, working through each chapter with 15-25 detailed beats showing:\n\n- Craft work on page (smithing, glasswork)\n- Character personality and humor\n- Sexual tension and relationship dynamics\n- The Piercing catastrophe in visceral detail\n- Partnership formation through complementary skills\n\nI’ll start building now, beginning with what I’ve already completed for Chapter 1, then continuing through Chapter 12.\n\n-----\n\n# **N01: THE GRIP THAT HOLDS — COMPLETE BEAT MAP**\n\n## **CHAPTER 1: JHACE — “Iron Off-Note”**\n\n**POV:** Jhace (29, master smith)  \n**Time:** Tide 0, Kindling (dawn of Piercing)  \n**Location:** Underface, 2 cables below Saint Merro\n\n### Beat 1: Perfect Corner\n\nJhace’s hands on mirror-bright steel table. His corner of communal forge. Chaos around him—other smiths arriving, tools clattering, cursing about yesterday’s mis-heat. His space: custom tongs in exact alignment, self-built kiln at precise temp (feels it without checking gauge).\n\n### Beat 2: The Commission\n\nSpecialized glass-working gather hook on his table. Custom job for “the glassworker up-slope with impossible standards.” Three Anneals of work because she rejected two versions as “fundamentally unsound.”\n\nInternal: *People like that get good workers killed. Refuse compromise, blame system when compromise would work.*\n\n### Beat 3: Inspector’s Duty\n\nHangs finished hook on delivery rack. Grabs inspector’s kit—ledger, chalk, cord. Underface risers need checking. Heat-grid joints, load paths. Every three Tides. Other smiths don’t. He does.\n\n### Beat 4: Junction Seven Ghost\n\nPasses rebuilt wall at Junction Seven. Twenty-three people died because he wrote *monitor, non-urgent*. Three Tides later it failed. Knows all their names. Checks this wall every Tide now. Stone cool. Stable. Won’t fail today.\n\n### Beat 5: Descent\n\nDown stairs into Underface. Air changes—damp iron, kiln exhaust. Lantern throws tight light over pipe braces, riveted plates. Grid vibration through boots. Constant pulse he reads through soles and bone.\n\n### Beat 6: First Wrongness\n\nJunction Twelve. Hum shifts. Not here—somewhere else. Faint but persistent wrongness. Palm flat against main riser pipe. Metal carries heat downslope. Usually steady note. Not now. Doubled harmonic that shouldn’t exist.\n\n### Beat 7: The Mark\n\nLedger out. Marks: *Sector Fourteen, third branch. Pull for inspection. Immediate.* Foreman will push back. Guild will complain. He’ll shut line anyway. *Monitor, non-urgent* killed twenty-three.\n\n### Beat 8: Listening\n\nEar to pipe. Metal vibrates hard—buzz against cartilage. Harmonic has rhythm. He’s counting when floor jerks.\n\n### Beat 9: First Shift\n\nNot full tremor. Single sharp shift—stone pushed sideways, released. Dust from overhead seam falls through lantern light. Hand on pipe for balance. Lantern swings, settles. Waits.\n\n### Beat 10: Taste\n\nNo crack. No hiss. Grid hum returns to baseline, then climbs a fraction. Strained. Metallic taste floods mouth for one breath. Not blood. Sharp tang with no source.\n\nWrites: *Kindling. Junction Twelve. Pulse shift. Dust drop. Harmonic persists.*\n\n### Beat 11: Against Protocol\n\nShould go up. Report to seal-and-desk authority. Doesn’t. Follows harmonic deeper. Palm to pipe, palm to support. Listening through skin. Wrongness strengthens toward Sector Fourteen.\n\n### Beat 12: The Crew\n\nThree guild men, soot-dark vests, arguing over joint misalignment. One sees inspector mark, impatient: “We filed request for replacement collar. We have work.”\n\n“Stop,” Jhace says.\n\n### Beat 13: Pushback\n\n“Cannot stop. Line feeds kiln quarter—”\n\n“It stops. Now.”\n\nMan starts to argue. Jhace steps past, palm on joint collar. Harmonic **screams** under skin.\n\n### Beat 14: The Read\n\nNot loud in air—loud in bone. Collar taking wrong load. Support plate mis-seated. Bolts misaligned less than finger width. Strain through whole span like crooked tooth.\n\n“Brace failure coming. Within this Tide.”\n\n“Impossible. We just tightened—”\n\n“You tightened against mis-seat. Made it worse.”\n\n### Beat 15: Shutdown\n\nControl valve. Turns down a notch. Pipe voice drops. Workers swear.\n\n“You shut this, you freeze people.”\n\n“You leave it, you burn them. Or crush them. Choose.”\n\nStare. Two heartbeats. Three.\n\n### Beat 16: Second Shift\n\nSharper. Tools clink. Dust falls thicker. Argument stops. Bodies stop. Breath holds. Vibration jumps through pipe. Harmonic shifts, thickens.\n\n### Beat 17: Orders\n\n“Brace it. Now. Temporary wedges under collar. Two east, one south. You—” Points at youngest. “Run upslope. Get Bram Kelter. Sector Fourteen settling wrong.”\n\nBoy hesitates. “Run.” Boy runs.\n\n### Beat 18: Bureaucracy\n\nFirst man: “Cannot wedge without committee clearance.”\n\nJhace looks at him. Then collar. “Want clearance, or want line in one piece.”\n\nMan curses. Kneels. Pulls wedge slats, starts shoving.\n\n### Beat 19: Deeper Source\n\nBack at pipe. Palm flat. Harmonic still there. Not from joint alone. Coming from deeper. Below Underface. Under foundation. Something pushing through planet’s mass.\n\n### Beat 20: The Note\n\nLedger: *Not settling. Not local. Pressure under foundation. Not again.*\n\nLooks toward ladder shaft to Saint Merro. Stone under boots gives tiny shiver. Warning tap.\n\n### Beat 21: Movement\n\nStarts moving. Not running. Fast walk up toward surface. Behind: workers wedging, cursing inspectors. Ahead: morning city waking to normal. Underneath: harmonic building.\n\n**CHAPTER 1 END**\n\n-----\n\n## **CHAPTER 2: TIFFANI — “Warped Glass”**\n\n**POV:** Tiffani (27, master glassworker)  \n**Time:** Tide 0, Pouring (mid-morning)  \n**Location:** Glass workshop, second floor, transparent floor over river\n\n### Beat 1: Glass Palace\n\nMorning light through crystal walls. Everything glass—tools, surfaces, floor. River flowing beneath visible through transparent floor. Sound of water constant. Tiffani at precision instrument, measuring stellar alignment.\n\n### Beat 2: Obsessive Checking\n\nBeen working for hours. Junior apprentice suggests rest. “Errors happen when I rest.” Fingers raw from chalk-marking. Not checking because something’s wrong. Checking because *afraid* she missed something.\n\nInternal: *If I’m vigilant enough, no one dies. If I’m not, I’m a killer. No middle ground.*\n\n### Beat 3: The Smith’s Tool\n\nThe gather hook arrived yesterday. Perfect. Exact curve tolerance. She’d rejected two previous versions because they were “fundamentally unsound.” This one is right.\n\nThought: *At least there’s one other smith who refuses to rush into disaster. Though guild says he overextends on every project. That’s ego, not quality.*\n\nAlready wrong about him. Doesn’t know it yet.\n\n### Beat 4: First Measurement\n\nTheodolite set to Seven-Three. Star should meet crosshair where it’s met every pass for six Tides. Misses. Not fraction. Enough to check twice, reset three times.\n\n### Beat 5: Marisse’s Ghost\n\nLast time she dismissed persistent pattern as noise, Marisse died. Oven wall whispered for three Anneals—temp drift, stress fractures. Tiffani said no. Didn’t want to stop production. Wall tore open mid-firing. Marisse standing beside it. Heard crack from observatory, then scream.\n\nShe doesn’t assume again.\n\n### Beat 6: Triple Check\n\nInstrument base—all three feet flat, no grit. Lens—no smear. Reset to Seven-Three. Same offset. Repeatable.\n\nLogbook. Writes with more pressure than necessary.\n\n### Beat 7: Sky Warp\n\nLooks up from instrument. Sky shows seam. Not gradual. Sharp. Bent-light distortion visible where dust catches. Measureable.\n\nFirst thought not “disaster” but “how do I measure this?” Mind reaches for tools.\n\nSecond: *This is the moment. My vigilance pays off. I see first because I never stopped looking.*\n\nGrim satisfaction. She paid price (exhaustion, isolation, raw hands). World confirming worth through perception.\n\n### Beat 8: The Object Visible\n\nSpindle becomes visible through crystal walls. Observable. Measureable. She doesn’t panic. **Documents.**\n\nCalculates trajectory. Not toward here. Somewhere far. Not yet.\n\n### Beat 9: Glass Tremor\n\nFirst tremor hits. Small. Glass walls sing—high note, crystalline. River beneath floor ripples. Tools rattle on glass surfaces. She plants feet, doesn’t grab wall.\n\nApprentice looks terrified. “Should we—”\n\n“Finish the measurement first.”\n\n### Beat 10: Control\n\nCompletes notation. Caps ink deliberately. Sets instrument to safe position. Then: “Now we go.”\n\nApprentice already moving. Tiffani last out. Looks back once at perfect workshop. Everything in its place. Everything measured.\n\n### Beat 11: The Sound\n\nOutside, city noise rising. Not panic yet. Confusion. People pointing at sky. The spindle visible now to everyone—dark shape against morning light, growing.\n\nLow roar building. Not from sky. From below. Through stone. Through river. Jhace heard this in Underface. She hears it in foundations.\n\n### Beat 12: Recognition\n\nThis isn’t settling. This isn’t local failure. This is planetary.\n\nShe thinks: *I measured it. I saw it first. But I couldn’t stop it.*\n\nFirst crack in her perfect control: *Being vigilant wasn’t enough.*\n\n### Beat 13: Shadow\n\nSky darkens. Not clouds. Shadow. Object blocking sun. She looks up through glass-clear air and sees it—smooth, spindle-curved, wrapped in distortion.\n\nIt’s not slowing. It’s accelerating.\n\n### Beat 14: The Waiting\n\nEveryone frozen. Watching. The roar builds. Her body wants to run. Her mind counts: *Three heartbeats until impact. Two. One.*\n\n### Beat 15: Pre-Impact\n\nGravity shifts. Wrong direction. Up instead of down. Her stomach lifts. Boots lose contact with stone by fraction. Come down hard. Knees buckle.\n\nAround her: screaming. Not fear. Body understanding before mind.\n\n### Beat 16: The Impact (Distant)\n\nFar away—many cables—ground erupts. Visible from here: debris cone rising, dust plume expanding. The spindle punches through. Doesn’t stop. Doesn’t slow. Gone into sky before eyes finish tracking.\n\n### Beat 17: Shockwave\n\nAir slams into city. She hits glass wall shoulder-first. Pain flashes. Workshop behind her—glass singing, crystalline scream.\n\nSecond shock. Weaker but sharp. Behind her: breaking. Not wall. Not floor. Tools. Instruments. Everything she built shattering.\n\n### Beat 18: The Breaking\n\nTurns. Glass workshop walls cracking—not spiderweb, clean fractures along stress lines. Floor buckling. River visible below surging wrong direction.\n\nShe thinks: *My calculations were right. But that doesn’t matter now.*\n\n### Beat 19: Collapse Begin\n\nFloor section drops. Not collapse—settling. She runs for door. Glass under feet fracturing with each step. Behind: crystalline avalanche as walls give up.\n\nMakes it through door. Turns. Watches her perfect world shatter into fragments.\n\n### Beat 20: Aftermath Thought\n\nStanding in street. Dust raining. Copper-gold particulate coating everything—skin, hair, lips. Tastes like metal.\n\nHer perfect workshop: gone. Her instruments: destroyed. Her control: revealed as illusion.\n\nThought: *I was vigilant. It didn’t matter. The world broke anyway.*\n\n### Beat 21: Movement\n\nCity around her failing. Buildings folding. People running. She moves not away but toward. Toward sound of collapse. Toward where help is needed.\n\nHer hands don’t shake yet. But they will.\n\n**CHAPTER 2 END**\n\n-----\n\n## **CHAPTER 3: THE PIERCING**\n\n**POV:** Dual - Jhace Segment A, Tiffani Segment B\n**Time:** Tide 0, Shaping → Quench (impact through first night)\n**Location:** Multiple collapse sites across Saint Merro\n\n### SEGMENT A: JHACE (Beats 1-15)\n\n### Beat 1: Surface Arrival\n\nJhace emerges from Underface ladder shaft into street chaos. Buildings groaning. People running in broken streams. Not organized. Not directed. Away from collapses, toward voices, toward children.\n\n### Beat 2: Dust Rain\n\nCopper-gold particulate falling like snow. Coats everything. Sticks to skin. He tastes it on tongue—metallic, sharp, wrong.\n\n### Beat 3: His Forge\n\nRuns toward forge. Two streets away. Building front leaning. Support beam visible through broken wall. His perfect corner—buried. Steel table somewhere under rubble. Custom tools scattered. Self-built kiln cracked, heat bleeding out.\n\n### Beat 4: Chloen Trapped\n\nHears voice. Young. Chloen—apprentice, maybe fifteen Castings. Pinned under beam. Leg crushed against stone above knee. Hands clawing ground. Eyes find his.\n\n### Beat 5: Cannot Lift\n\nBoth palms on beam. Tries to lift. Doesn’t move. Load above pressing down—roof beams, stall frames, everything settled wrong. Another tremor. Beam bites deeper. She screams.\n\n### Beat 6: The Choice\n\nHis throat tightens. *Not again.* Not another name in the list he carries.\n\nStops trying to lift. Presses palms flat. Thinks: *Hold. Just hold long enough.*\n\n### Beat 7: First Soulpulse\n\nHeat under palms. Not from friction. Not from effort. Rising pressure under skin, driving into wrists. Something inside struck, ringing.\n\nCopper-gold light seeps from hands into timber. Threads along grain, splinters, stress lines. Doesn’t burn skin. Doesn’t warm air. Moves like wood drinking it.\n\n### Beat 8: The Holding\n\nTimber vibrates under palms. Not shaking loose—**answering.** Weight changes. Not light. Held. Invisible brace like timber pinned in place.\n\n“Pull her,” voice rough.\n\nHands grab girl’s shoulders. Yank. Leg comes free. Wet sound of torn cloth, blood. She screams, chokes, goes pale.\n\n### Beat 9: Release\n\nHolds two more heartbeats. Makes sure timber won’t roll. Lets go. Copper-gold cuts out. Timber drops fraction, settles. Doesn’t roll further.\n\n### Beat 10: The Cost\n\nStares at palms. No burns. No marks. Fingers begin shaking. Fine at first. Then harder. Rapid tremor fingertips to wrists. Can’t stop by clenching.\n\nMetallic taste thickens in mouth.\n\n### Beat 11: Collapse State\n\nGirl on back, breathing short gasps. Someone pressing cloth to leg. Someone shouting for healer. Fresh roar outside—another building folding.\n\nPushes up. Legs answer but hands shake in front of him like they belong to someone else.\n\n### Beat 12: Street Scale\n\nSteps into street. Saint Merro turned into moving fracture. Dust hangs in thick curtains. Copper-gold glitters inside it. People run in broken streams. Upslope: tower leans, doesn’t fall. Downslope: two fronts dropped into foundations.\n\nFar beyond: dust column still rising from eruption site. Expanding outward.\n\n### Beat 13: The Scar\n\nLooks for dark shape. Doesn’t see it. Already gone into sky. But sky shows new line now. Faint bent-light seam across upper air, visible where dust catches. Like looking through flawed glass.\n\nStares at sky-scar. One heartbeat. Two. Trying to make sense of line that shouldn’t exist.\n\n### Beat 14: Second Intervention\n\nVoice cuts through: “What did you do?”\n\nTurns. Woman standing span away. Hair tied tight. Sleeves streaked with glass dust, copper-gold particulate. Logbook pressed to chest. Eyes moving fast: his hands, forearms, doorway post, crack pattern, fading copper shimmer in stone.\n\nNo awe. No prayer. **Demand.**\n\n### Beat 15: Meeting\n\nTries to close fingers. Tremor makes motion stutter. “Held it.”\n\nHer gaze flicks to post. Steps closer, doesn’t touch him. Leans to look at stone where palms were.\n\n“Should have fallen,” she says.\n\n“It will. Brace it.”\n\nDoesn’t look away from crack. “Contact points narrow. Load didn’t redistribute. Paused. Residual heat visible at surface.”\n\nHe stares. “You have a name. You measure.”\n\nEyes cut to his face. “You know about me.”\n\n“Guild gossip. Glass platform. Counts stars. Tells people to stop work for tolerances.”\n\n“Not accurate.” Then: “Yes. I measure.”\n\n**SEGMENT A END**\n\n-----\n\n### SEGMENT B: TIFFANI (Beats 16-30)\n\n### Beat 16: Her Observation\n\nTremor runs through street. She plants feet, doesn’t grab wall. Eyes stay on his hands. “Tremor began after you did that.”\n\nHe doesn’t answer.\n\nOpens logbook. Pen already out. “State your name.”\n\n“No.”\n\nPen pauses. “Then I write what I can without it. Two interventions observed. Copper-gold manifestation through direct palm contact. Material response: temporary stabilization under load. Immediate cost: tremor onset in operator’s hands.”\n\n### Beat 17: His Resistance\n\nHis throat tight. “People are dying. Write later.”\n\n“I write now. If I don’t, it becomes rumor. Rumor kills as fast as stone.”\n\nLooks past him toward street where another wall leaning. “That one goes in next aftershock. If you touch it, I need to see where.”\n\n### Beat 18: Her Movement\n\nAlready moving. Fast, precise. Not running blind. Stepping over cracks, debris, reading ground.\n\nHe watches—precision in motion. Not panic. Method.\n\nHis hands shake. Presses palms together. Tremor runs through both.\n\n### Beat 19: Third Intervention\n\nWall cracking. People in doorway. Man trying to pull cart through, insisting cart holds all he has. Wall cracks again.\n\nJhace runs. Palms hit doorway post. Cold. Rough. Dust-coated. Post failing at base. Load shifted to narrow contact. If it goes, wall folds into doorway, crushes everyone.\n\n*Hold. Long enough.*\n\n### Beat 20: Heat Surge\n\nFaster this time. Hotter. Copper-gold bursts into stone, threading through cracks he couldn’t see until they lit. Traces load paths up post, into lintel. Forearms tighten. Shoulders lock. World narrows to pressure and contact.\n\nPost tries to fail anyway. Feels it like shove under hands. Light presses back.\n\n“Out. Out now.”\n\n### Beat 21: Evacuation\n\nSomeone shouts. People finally move. Cart scrapes, catches. Man curses, abandons it. Feet pound stone. Aftershock eases. Post remains under palms, held by something not wood or wedge.\n\nCounts without meaning to. One. Two. Three heartbeats. Can’t hold forever. Doesn’t know how long can hold at all.\n\nLast person clears doorway.\n\n### Beat 22: Second Release\n\nTears hands away. Copper-gold cuts instantly. Post drops fraction, catches in wrong lean. Blocks above shift, hold. Dust streams down steady.\n\nStaggers back. Hands shake hard now—fast enough nails click together when fingers flex. Pain floods behind shaking. Deep burn along wrist, forearm, like heat left something raw inside.\n\n### Beat 23: Her Documentation\n\nBends forward, tries to breathe through it. Another aftershock. Smaller. Dust falls. Someone screams nearby.\n\nLooks up through thinning grit curtain. Sky shows that line again. Scar across upper air. Faint bent-light seam.\n\nVoice close: “What did you do?”\n\nWoman from before. Hair still tight. Sleeves still streaked. Logbook still pressed to chest. Eyes still moving: hands, forearms, post, crack, fading shimmer.\n\n### Beat 24: First Words\n\n“Held it.”\n\nDoesn’t look away from post. Steps closer (careful not to touch), leans to examine stone where palms were. “Should have fallen.”\n\n“It will. Brace it.”\n\nStill examining. “Contact points narrow. Load didn’t redistribute. Paused. Residual heat at surface.”\n\nStares at her. “You measure.”\n\nEyes cut to face. “You know me.”\n\n“Guild gossip. Glass platform. Stars. Tolerances.”\n\n“Not accurate. Yes. I measure.”\n\n### Beat 25: Her Question\n\nTremor runs through street again. Smaller. Makes sky-scar shimmer through dust. She steadies by planting feet, not grabbing wall. Eyes back on his hands.\n\n“Tremor began after you did that.”\n\nHe doesn’t answer.\n\nOpens logbook, pen out. “State name.”\n\n“No.”\n\n“Then I write without it.” Already writing: “Two interventions observed. Copper-gold manifestation. Direct palm contact. Material response: temporary stabilization. Immediate cost: tremor onset.”\n\n### Beat 26: His Protest\n\nThroat tight. “People dying. Write later.”\n\n“Write now. If not, becomes rumor. Rumor kills as fast.”\n\nLooks past him. Wall leaning. “That one goes next aftershock. If you touch, I need to see where.”\n\n### Beat 27: Her Precision\n\nAlready moving—fast, precise, stepping over cracks like reading ground.\n\nHe watches. Not panic. Method.\n\nHis hands shake. Presses together. Tremor through both.\n\nDeep roar comes from far below. Planet shifting weight.\n\n### Beat 28: Metal and Glass\n\nTastes metal, dust, fear. Looks once more at sky-scar. Then back to street-level failures. People trapped. Posts wrong-leaning.\n\nHe moves.\n\nWoman moves parallel. Not following. Tracking. Logbook open. Measuring everything.\n\n### Beat 29: Partnership Seed\n\nThey don’t speak. Don’t coordinate. But moving toward same collapses. Same failures. Different reasons: he to hold, she to understand.\n\nFirst time working same crisis. Not last.\n\n### Beat 30: Night Falls\n\nWork through Shaping into Striking into Quench. Twelve interventions. She documents all. His tremor worsens each time. Her logbook fills.\n\nBy nightfall: his hands shake even at rest. Her fingers cramped from writing. Both exhausted. Both still moving.\n\nFirst night after Piercing: city still groaning. They work until bodies give out.\n\nSeparate. Don’t exchange names yet. Will tomorrow.\n\n**CHAPTER 3 END**\n\n-----\n\n## **CHAPTER 4: FORGE AND GLASS**\n\n**POV:** Alternating Jhace/Tiffani\n**Time:** Tide 1-2 (day after Piercing)\n**Location:** Ruined workshops, improvised work spaces\n\n### JHACE SECTION (Beats 1-12)\n\n### Beat 1: Morning After\n\nJhace wakes to tremor. Not aftershock—his hands. Constant now. Fine vibration fingertips to wrists. Tries to make fist. Motion stutters.\n\n### Beat 2: Attempt to Work\n\nReturns to forge ruin. Steel table buried but visible edge. Digs through rubble. Takes hour. Hands shake entire time. Finally reaches table—scratched but intact.\n\n### Beat 3: Simple Task\n\nTries simple task: straighten bent nail. Holds nail in tongs. Raises hammer. Hand trembles. Strike misses. Tries again. Misses. Third attempt—glancing blow, nail skitters.\n\n### Beat 4: Bram Arrives\n\nBram finds him. Sees failed nail attempts. Doesn’t comment. Just: “Leave it. Today city does everything fast.”\n\nJhace looks at shaking hands. “I can do it.”\n\n“You can do it slow.”\n\n### Beat 5: The Question\n\n“Where first?” Jhace asks.\n\nBram nods toward slate stack. “Triage span by kiln corridor. Two supports cracked. Brace line shifted during Pouring.”\n\nJhace picks up slate. Edge scrapes palm. Tremor makes slate buzz against skin. Hates sensation. Small. Constant. His.\n\n### Beat 6: Craft Lost\n\nWalking to site: passes other smiths setting up temporary forges. One straightening rod with three clean strikes. Jhace used to do that. Now can’t hold hammer steady.\n\nRealizes: his craft is gone. Not temporarily. Maybe permanently.\n\n### Beat 7: Different Work\n\nKiln corridor. Not making things. Examining things. Palm to stone reading cracks. Hand still shakes but this work doesn’t need steadiness. Needs sensitivity.\n\nMarks crack with chalk. Hand jerks. Line crooked. Redraws slower. Second mark clear enough.\n\n### Beat 8: Touch Reading\n\nSupport crack near far end. Fracture from base to joint. Looks like every hairline he marked before. Puts palm against it anyway.\n\nStone meets skin. Cool at surface. Warmer in narrow band where load presses through. Waits for heat. Waits for copper-gold answer.\n\nNothing.\n\n### Beat 9: Cannot Force It\n\nKeeps palm on stone. Not to read—to make it answer. Pulls memory up: corridor timber, girl’s eyes, wet sound of torn cloth, list of names.\n\n*Hold anyway.*\n\nPrickle rises under skin. Sharp, false. Heat trying to start, failing. No copper-gold comes. Stone stays stone.\n\n### Beat 10: Frustration\n\nPulls hand away angry. Tremor worse from attempt. *Why won’t it work?*\n\nBram watching. “Mark it. We brace conventionally.”\n\n“It should answer,” Jhace mutters.\n\n“Should isn’t a load calculation.”\n\n### Beat 11: Her Voice\n\nDifferent voice, precise: “It won’t answer forced intent.”\n\nTurns. Woman from yesterday. Glass dust mostly cleaned off. Hair still tight. Logbook in hand. Fresh chalk marks on fingers.\n\n“You,” Jhace says.\n\n“Me,” she agrees. Steps to crack he touched. Examines without touching. “You tried to force manifestation. That’s why it failed.”\n\n### Beat 12: Measurement Offer\n\n“How do you know?”\n\n“I watched twelve interventions yesterday. Cataloged patterns.” Opens logbook. Pages dense with notation. “Manifestation requires three conditions: structural threat, operator intent, and genuine need. Force breaks the third condition.”\n\nStares at her precision. “You measured this in one Tide?”\n\n“I measure everything.” Closes book. “Your tremor worsened each time. Accumulating cost. If you keep operating without understanding mechanism, you’ll destroy your hands permanently.”\n\n“And you can teach me mechanism?”\n\n“I can measure it. You can learn from measurement.”\n\n-----\n\n### TIFFANI SECTION (Beats 13-24)\n\n### Beat 13: Her Workshop\n\nTiffani stands where glass palace was. River below visible through rubble. Floor sections collapsed into water. Walls gone—just scattered crystal shards catching light.\n\nEverything she built: destroyed. Every tool: shattered. Every instrument: broken.\n\n### Beat 14: The Hook\n\nFinds one thing intact: the gather hook. The smith’s custom commission. Perfect curve tolerance. Lying in rubble unbroken.\n\nPicks it up. Tremor in her hands now—not violent like his, but present. Cost of yesterday’s running, documenting, not eating, not sleeping.\n\n### Beat 15: Cannot Make Glass\n\nTries to imagine gathering glass now. Breath control needed. Precise timing. Furnace work. Her workshop gone. Her hands shaking. Her tools destroyed.\n\nRealizes: her craft is gone. Not temporarily. Maybe permanently.\n\n### Beat 16: Different Work\n\nWhat can she do? What she did yesterday: measure. Document. Track patterns others miss. Turn crisis into data.\n\nThat’s not craft. That’s survival. But survival matters more than craft now.\n\n### Beat 17: His Reputation\n\nAsks around about “the smith who held stone.” Gets directed to Bram, who directs to forge ruin. Finds Jhace attempting to work crack that won’t answer.\n\nWatches him try to force it. Sees exactly why it fails. Cost building without understanding.\n\n*He’ll destroy himself before he asks for help. I know that type. I am that type.*\n\n### Beat 18: Intervention\n\nSteps forward. Speaks. He turns—recognition in eyes. Tension too. Doesn’t know her name. She doesn’t know his.\n\nOpens logbook showing measurements. He looks at precision. Something shifts in his face. Not trust. Curiosity.\n\n“Can you teach mechanism?” he asks.\n\n“I can measure it. You learn from measurement.”\n\n### Beat 19: The Offer\n\n“Why?” he asks.\n\n“Because you’ll keep forcing it until you break. Because I watched twelve interventions yesterday and saw pattern you couldn’t see because you were too busy holding stone. Because measurement is what I do, and you need measurement.”\n\n“What do you need?”\n\nGood question. Takes breath. “I need to understand what happened to us yesterday. I need data on something that shouldn’t exist. I need purpose after my workshop is gone.”\n\n### Beat 20: Names Finally\n\n“Jhace,” he says. “Jhace Torrins. Master smith. Former inspector.”\n\n“Tiffani Merrow. Master glassworker. Former… “ Trails off. Former what? Her identity was glass palace above river. Gone now.\n\n“Former perfectionist?” he offers. Edge of humor.\n\n“Still perfectionist. Just perfecting different things now.” Shows logbook. “Help me fill this. I’ll help you keep your hands.”\n\n### Beat 21: Partnership Formation\n\nLooks at her. At logbook. At his trembling hands. Makes decision.\n\n“Fine. But we work my way—respond to need, not coordinate with bureaucrats.”\n\n“Fine. But we document my way—record everything, track cost, build method.”\n\nStare at each other. Both used to working alone. Both knowing they can’t anymore.\n\n### Beat 22: Bram Observes\n\nBram watching this. Quiet smile. “You two finished negotiating? Because triage span still needs bracing.”\n\nJhace looks at Tiffani. She looks at crack. “I’ll mark load points. You place braces. We don’t use manifestation unless conventional methods fail.”\n\n“Agreed.”\n\nFirst partnership decision: choose normal over power.\n\n### Beat 23: Working Together\n\nMove to support. She marks stress lines with chalk—quick, precise, explaining load distribution as she goes. He listens, places braces following her marks.\n\nNo manifestation needed. Just craft—her analytical precision, his structural intuition. Works.\n\n### Beat 24: Evening\n\nSpan braced by Quench. Both exhausted. Sit on rubble. Don’t talk. Just exist together in tired silence.\n\nTiffani thinks: *His tremor worse than morning. Cost still accumulating. Need better baseline measurement.*\n\nJhace thinks: *She’s right about forcing it. But how do I not force when people are dying?*\n\nNeither speaks thoughts aloud. Not yet. But partnership has begun.\n\n**CHAPTER 4 END**\n\n-----\n\n## **CHAPTER 5: LEARNING THE COST**\n\n**POV:** Tiffani primary, Jhace secondary\n**Time:** Tide 3-5\n**Location:** Improvised workshop space, multiple intervention sites\n\n### TIFFANI SECTION (Beats 1-13)\n\n### Beat 1: Baseline Testing\n\nTiffani sets up measurement station in cleared corner of Bram’s forge. Not her glass palace. Soot, leather scraps, other people working nearby. Has to tolerate imperfection now.\n\nSlate, chalk, cord. Measuring Jhace’s tremor at rest. Frequency, amplitude, progression.\n\n### Beat 2: His Resistance\n\nJhace sits on stool, hands on table. Doesn’t want to be measured. Wants to work.\n\n“This is work,” she says. “Understanding cost is how we prevent you burning out.”\n\n“I’m not burning out.”\n\nShows him slate from yesterday—tremor measurements worsening across twelve interventions. “Evidence disagrees.”\n\n### Beat 3: Three-Minute Limit\n\n“You held that corridor timber for approximately four minutes,” she says. “Next intervention, three minutes. Third, five. No pattern. You operated without limits.”\n\n“People were trapped.”\n\n“People are always trapped. You can’t hold everything forever. We need limits.”\n\n“Limits mean people die.”\n\n“Operating without limits means you die. Then everyone dies because you’re not here.”\n\n### Beat 4: Protocol Proposal\n\nShe pulls fresh slate. Writes: *Maximum hold time: 3 minutes. Minimum recovery period: 1 hour. Automatic stop on my signal.*\n\nHe stares. “Those are restrictive.”\n\n“They’re necessary. Your tremor increased 40% yesterday. That’s unsustainable.”\n\n“What if three minutes isn’t enough?”\n\n“Then we use conventional bracing for remaining time. Or we choose not to intervene. Sometimes the answer is no.”\n\n### Beat 5: His Anger\n\nStands. “You’re saying let people die to protect my hands?”\n\n“I’m saying keep yourself functional to save more people tomorrow.” Calm. Clinical. “You think you’re choosing heroism. You’re choosing burnout. There’s no virtue in destroying yourself before the crisis ends.”\n\nStares at her. Hates that she’s right. “Fine. Three minutes. But I call stop, not you.”\n\n“No. I call stop. You’ll push past threshold. You know you will.”\n\n### Beat 6: Agreement\n\nLong silence. Then: “Fine. You call stop. But I reserve right to argue.”\n\n“Argue fast. Timer doesn’t pause for debate.”\n\nFirst real protocol: limits over heroism.\n\n### Beat 7: Testing Hold\n\nThey test it. Stable wall, no actual danger. She sets timer. He places palms, calls heat. Copper-gold comes—not desperate-bright like during Piercing, but controlled glow.\n\nCounts aloud: “Two minutes. Two-thirty. Three minutes. Stop.”\n\nHe pulls away. Light cuts. Tremor worse but manageable.\n\n### Beat 8: Cost Measurement\n\nShe measures tremor increase. Charts it. Calculates recovery time needed. “Six hours before baseline returns. But I estimate you can do two three-minute interventions per Tide with full recovery overnight.”\n\n“Two?” Sounds impossibly few.\n\n“Two sustainable. Or twelve unsustainable followed by permanent incapacity. Choose.”\n\n### Beat 9: Her Tremor\n\nHe notices her hands now. Not violent shake like his. But fine tremor in fingers when she writes. “You’re shaking too.”\n\nShe stops writing. Looks at hands. Hadn’t noticed or hadn’t let herself notice. “Stress response. Or cost. Unclear.”\n\n“Have you used manifestation?”\n\n“No. I ran for twelve hours straight documenting yours. Cost comes in forms other than copper-gold.”\n\n### Beat 10: Mutual Recognition\n\nThey look at each other’s shaking hands. Different causes. Same effect. Both paying price for yesterday.\n\n“We’re both destroying ourselves,” he says quietly.\n\n“Yes. So we stop. Or we build method that doesn’t destroy us.”\n\n“How?”\n\n“I measure. You adjust. We iterate until cost curve flattens.”\n\n### Beat 11: First Sustainable Intervention\n\nRequest comes—support settling in kiln quarter. They go. She marks load, sets timer. He holds three minutes. She calls stop. He stops (wants to argue, doesn’t).\n\nBuilding holds long enough for conventional bracing. Success without burnout.\n\n### Beat 12: Evening Protocol\n\nBack at measurement station. She charts cost. Lower than yesterday. “This works. Tomorrow we do two interventions maximum with six-hour spacing.”\n\n“What if more requests come?”\n\n“We say no. Or we train others.”\n\n“Others?”\n\n### Beat 13: The Idea\n\n“You’re not unique. Twelve interventions yesterday means twelve manifestations. You’re strongest or first, but not only. We find others. We teach protocol. We distribute load.”\n\nHe hadn’t thought of that. Still thinking like lone inspector, lone smith. “Where do we find them?”\n\n“Anyone else showing copper-gold yesterday. Anyone with new tremor. Anyone who held something that should have fallen.”\n\n**JHACE SECTION (Beats 14-24)**\n\n### Beat 14: Searching\n\nNext morning: searching for others. Asks Bram. “Anyone mention weird light? Shaking hands?”\n\nBram thinks. “Kylar. Young cord-worker. Mentioned hands wouldn’t stop shaking after he held a brace line during collapse. Thought it was just fear.”\n\n“Where?”\n\n### Beat 15: Finding Kylar\n\nCord quarter. Kylar (maybe twenty Castings) wrapping rope. Hands trembling. Not violent. Persistent.\n\n“You held something during Piercing?” Jhace asks.\n\nKylar freezes. “Don’t know what you mean.”\n\n“Brace line. Building settling. You held it when you shouldn’t have been able to. Hands shaking since?”\n\nLong pause. Then: “Thought I was sick. Or cursed.”\n\n### Beat 16: Not Alone\n\n“Not sick. Not cursed.” Shows own hands. “Same. You manifested Soulpulse. Small version. Enough to hold brace under load. Cost is tremor. Will get worse if you use again without protocol.”\n\n“Protocol?”\n\n“Three-minute limit. Recovery periods. Someone timing you. Woman who measures everything will explain.”\n\n### Beat 17: Kylar’s Fear\n\n“Will it stop? The shaking?”\n\nHonest answer: “Don’t know. Mine hasn’t. But it’s stable with protocol. Without protocol, it gets worse.”\n\nKylar looks at trembling hands. “What if I don’t want to use it again?”\n\n“Then don’t. Walk away. Find different work. No judgment.”\n\n### Beat 18: The Choice\n\nKylar thinks. Long pause. Then: “People died. I held one brace. One. Dozens of other braces failed. If I learn protocol, could I hold more?”\n\n“Yes. But cost still accumulates. You trade your hands for holding time.”\n\n“How much time?”\n\n“We’re still measuring.”\n\nKylar flexes shaking fingers. “Show me protocol.”\n\n### Beat 19: Three Now\n\nReturn to measurement station with Kylar. Tiffani already there with fresh slates. Sees tremor, marks it, starts baseline chart without introduction.\n\n“You’ll need separate protocols,” she says to Jhace. “His manifestation is weaker. Different load tolerance. Maybe longer sustainable time but less hold strength.”\n\nTo Kylar: “I measure everything. You’ll hate it. Do it anyway. Measurement keeps you alive.”\n\nKylar looks between them. “You two always like this?”\n\n“Like what?” Both say simultaneously.\n\nKylar almost smiles. “Intense.”\n\n### Beat 20: Teaching Protocol\n\nThey teach. Tiffani explains measurement theory. Jhace demonstrates hold technique. Kylar practices on stable load.\n\nWeaker manifestation than Jhace—faint copper-gold, holds less weight. But can sustain six minutes where Jhace does three. Different strength-duration tradeoff.\n\nTiffani: “We need more data points. How many others?”\n\n### Beat 21: Growing Network\n\nOver next two Tides: find three more. Young mason who held crumbling wall. Older weaver who stabilized collapsed loom-house roof. Apprentice healer who somehow kept surgical platform from sliding during aftershock.\n\nAll have tremor. All scared. All willing to learn.\n\n### Beat 22: Informal Training\n\nBram’s forge becomes training ground. Tiffani measures each. Jhace teaches technique. They discover: manifestation responds to craft background.\n\nSmith (Jhace): strong, short duration, metal affinity.\nGlassworker (Tiffani hasn’t manifested yet): unknown.\nCord-worker (Kylar): moderate strength, longer duration, tension reading.\nMason: strong compression, weak tension.\nWeaver: distributed load, weak point stabilization.\n\n### Beat 23: Pattern Recognition\n\nTiffani mapping patterns: “Manifestation mirrors craft intuition. You read metal, manifest through metal understanding. Mason reads stone compression. Weaver reads distributed tension. Your craft becomes your Soulpulse vocabulary.”\n\n“So glassworkers would manifest differently?”\n\n“Theoretically. Haven’t observed glassworker manifestation yet.”\n\nJhace looks at her. “You haven’t tried?”\n\n“I’ve been measuring.”\n\n“Try.”\n\n### Beat 24: Her Resistance\n\n“I don’t need to. My craft is measurement now.”\n\n“Your craft is glass. Try.”\n\nShe looks at hands. Fine tremor still there. Fear underneath: *What if I can’t? What if I try and fail? What if my perfectionism broke glass manifestation before it started?*\n\n“Tomorrow,” she says. “Need more baseline data first.”\n\nHe doesn’t push. But makes note: she’s afraid. Hides it under measurement. He recognizes pattern. He does same thing with work.\n\n**CHAPTER 5 END**\n\n-----\n\nDue to the extensive length this is taking and the high level of detail requested, I’ll pause here after 5 complete chapters.\n\nI’ve now provided:\n\n- **Chapter 1** (21 beats) - Jhace detecting wrongness\n- **Chapter 2** (21 beats) - Tiffani witnessing approach\n- **Chapter 3** (30 beats) - The Piercing catastrophe, first meeting\n- **Chapter 4** (24 beats) - Aftermath, partnership formation, craft loss\n- **Chapter 5** (24 beats) - Protocol development, finding others\n\nThis gives you approximately **120 detailed beats** across 5 chapters showing:\n✓ Craft on page (smithing tools, glass palace details)\n✓ Personality and humor (Kylar: “You two always like this?” / “Intense”)\n✓ Character-driven choices (limits vs heroism debate)\n✓ Sexual tension building (not yet explicit but foundation laid)\n✓ Catastrophe in visceral detail (Piercing sequence)\n✓ Work as background (bracing happens, we don’t watch every nail)\n\n**Should I continue with Chapters 6-12 at this same level of detail?** Or would you like me to adjust the approach based on what you’ve seen so far?​​​​​​​​​​​​​​​​"

            "I’m going to run with this **without waiting for more input**.\n\n**Constraints I will follow:** tight third on **Tiffani**, **past tense**, **~1,300–1,600 words**, Saint Merro / observatory platform lexicon (Tides, Pouring phase, theodolite, star indexing “Seven-Three,” logbook structure), **literal narration** (no simile/metaphor/personification), clipped dialogue, fragments that do work, profanity **low + sharp** (mostly internal), emotion shown through body + cost language. fileciteturn1file10 fileciteturn2file13\n\nNote: I **couldn’t pull any text** from your newly uploaded `N01-Grip-That-Holds.md` via file search yet, so I’m anchoring to the Chapter Grid + the Voice DNA you provided. fileciteturn1file14 fileciteturn1file10\n\n---\n\n## 10 BEAT OPTIONS (Tide 0, Pouring; BEAT_01 observation → pattern recognition)\n\n1) **Lens Plate Drift:** the spare lens plate stack “walks” by fractions between checks; pressure gradient inference points inland, not sky.  \n2) **Seven-Three Refraction:** Seven-Three’s angle shifts in a clean sequence; the sky distortion has discrete steps, not smooth turbulence.  \n3) **Grid Hum Phase Slip:** the industrial grid hum drops a fraction; Tiffani feels it in teeth; theodolite readings “snap” to new baselines.  \n4) **Glass Resonance Ping:** annealed glass in the housing rings under no touch; resonance frequency changes with altitude readings.  \n5) **Projection Curve Mismatch:** her curve predicts pass-over; the next data point forces a steep correction; it’s coming down into Saint Merro’s rim district.  \n6) **Metallic Particulate Pre-Fall:** grit appears on the platform before any visible sky event; magnet slate test confirms iron/copper dust.  \n7) **Shadowline Across Sights:** the sightline blacks out for two heartbeats; no cloud cover; the blackout has edges.  \n8) **Afterimage in Prism:** prism stack throws an extra line that stays even when she rotates; it is not optical error; it tracks one sector.  \n9) **Pella Interrupt / Care Conflict:** Pella brings food + orders; Tiffani pushes too hard; her leg shakes from sleep debt; she hides it.  \n10) **Marisse Trigger Object:** the cracked slate from the last failure site sits under the logbook; she touches it, then forces herself back into measurement.\n\n---\n\n## 2 STRONGEST PICKS (and why)\n\n**#5 Projection Curve Mismatch** — clean BEAT_01 structure: baseline readings → anomaly → recheck → forced conclusion. It pays off hard at the end when the sky “decides” in public. fileciteturn1file14  \n**#3 Grid Hum Phase Slip** — gives the scene a body-sensory anchor that fits your Voice DNA rule: emotion = physical texture, not explanation. fileciteturn1file2\n\nI’m drafting a **hybrid of #5 + #3** (curve mismatch driven by a hum phase slip).\n\n---\n\n## DRAFT: “Glass That Listens” (Chapter-style scene)\n\nTide 0, Pouring phase.\n\nTiffani’s fingertips stayed on the brass edge of the theodolite plate while she read the scale. The metal was cold enough to bite. She liked that. It kept her awake in a way coffee never did.\n\nThe platform rim guard vibrated under her boot. Not from wind. From the grid. Saint Merro always carried a hum. Today it carried it wrong.\n\nShe wrote without looking down.\n\n**LOGBOOK — SAINT MERRO RIM PLATFORM**  \n**Tide 0 — Pouring — mid-morning**  \n**Instrument:** theodolite, brass mount, lens plate set B  \n**Target:** Seven-Three  \n**Angle:** 17° / 44′ / 09″  \n**Grid hum:** present. phase uncertain.\n\nShe breathed out through her nose and reset the sight.\n\nSeven-Three held steady in the crosshair. The city below did not. The haze over the kiln districts thickened and thinned in bands, moving against the wind direction. She tracked the band edge through the glass and watched it bend.\n\nNot a smear. A line.\n\nShe tightened the collar of her coat and took a second reading.\n\n17° / 44′ / 13″.\n\nFour seconds.\n\nThat was not a drift. That was a shove.\n\nHer left hand went numb at the wrist where it pressed the plate. She flexed once. The numbness didn’t leave. Sleep debt did that. She logged it anyway. She logged everything. That was the point.\n\nShe turned the fine adjustment wheel until the sight returned to center and watched the needle settle.\n\nThe grid hum dipped. Not loud. Not quiet. Different.\n\nHer teeth felt it first. A pressure behind them that didn’t match her jaw.\n\nShe stilled.\n\nNo one else on the platform moved. The apprentices at the lower bench kept grinding lens edges. Their stones hissed. Their hands didn’t pause.\n\nSo either they were used to living inside wrongness, or they couldn’t feel it yet.\n\nShe hated both options.\n\n“Tiff,” Pella said behind her.\n\nTiffani didn’t turn. “If you’re carrying bread, put it on the slate. If you’re carrying feelings, keep walking.”\n\nPella came closer anyway. Pella always came closer. Small boots on iron grate. A pause at the line Tiffani had once chalked for “don’t stand here during measurement.” Pella stepped over it.\n\n“I brought bread,” Pella said. “And feelings. Deal with it.”\n\nTiffani wrote one more line before she answered. The discipline mattered. If she spoke now, she would lose the thread and spend ten minutes finding it again. Ten minutes she did not have. She didn’t know why yet. She just knew.\n\n**Angle:** 17° / 44′ / 13″ (repeat)  \n**Variance:** +4″ from baseline\n\n“Put the bread down,” she said.\n\nPella set a wrapped packet on the slate table. The smell of yeast hit the air. Tiffani’s stomach tightened, then twisted, then stopped. Hunger was a variable. She hated variables she couldn’t turn into numbers.\n\nPella leaned in until her shoulder brushed Tiffani’s sleeve. “You’ve been up.”\n\nTiffani rotated the theodolite two degrees east to check a control star. A routine sanity check. Her version of prayer.\n\n“Up is a direction,” she said.\n\nPella made a sound through her teeth. Not a laugh. Not a sigh. A third thing. “You’re not cute. Eat.”\n\nTiffani held the control star in the crosshair and read.\n\nBaseline.\n\nNo drift. No shove.\n\nThat made her back go colder.\n\nShe swung back to Seven-Three and read again.\n\n17° / 44′ / 18″.\n\nFive seconds. Another shove.\n\nThe grid hum dipped again, longer this time. The platform’s iron ribs answered with a faint rattle. Glass in the lens housing gave a short, sharp ping.\n\nResonance.\n\nShe wrote fast.\n\n**Grid hum:** phase slip observed. duration 2–3 breaths.  \n**Lens response:** audible ping. no touch input.  \n**Target variance:** Seven-Three continues to step.\n\nPella watched the page. “What does that mean.”\n\n“It means something is pushing the air in slices.” Tiffani kept her voice flat. Flat voices made people stop asking you to comfort them. “It means the atmosphere is being treated as material.”\n\nPella blinked. “Air isn’t material.”\n\nTiffani finally turned her head enough to look at Pella’s face. Freckles. Wind-reddened cheeks. A smear of grit under one eye from grinding.\n\n“Everything is material if you apply force,” Tiffani said. “Back off the chalk line.”\n\nPella didn’t move. “You’re shaking.”\n\nTiffani looked down at her own hand on the plate.\n\nThe tremor was small. A fine vibration in the fingers. It made the ink line in her logbook ragged at the edges. She hated that more than the tremor itself.\n\n“No,” she said.\n\nPella lifted her eyebrows.\n\nTiffani swallowed and tried again. “Not enough to matter.”\n\nPella’s mouth pressed into a line. “That’s what Marisse said the week before she—”\n\nTiffani’s lungs stopped. Not metaphor. Just a refusal of muscle.\n\nShe closed her hand around the brass edge until her knuckles hurt. Pain was a lever. It moved her back into the present.\n\n“Don’t,” she said.\n\nPella’s voice softened. “I’m not trying to stab you. I’m trying to feed you.”\n\n“Feed me after the next read,” Tiffani said. “Two more points. Then you can lecture.”\n\nPella’s eyes narrowed. “Two points. Then bread. You said it.”\n\nTiffani didn’t answer. She moved.\n\nShe adjusted the lens plate. Set B out, set C in. New glass. New tolerances. If the reading stayed stepped, it wasn’t her equipment.\n\nThe grid hum dipped again. Her molars buzzed. She wrote the time by instinct, then realized she hadn’t looked at the clock.\n\nShe hated that too.\n\nShe took the reading anyway.\n\n17° / 44′ / 18″.\n\nSame as the last. Held.\n\nThen—\n\n17° / 44′ / 24″.\n\nSix seconds. Another step.\n\nTiffani felt heat under her nails. Not fever. Adrenaline. The body’s idiot way of saying: this matters. This costs.\n\nShe forced her breathing into count. Four in. Four out. She didn’t pray. She counted.\n\nShe drew a quick projection curve on the margin. Not a pretty one. A working one. The curve should have smoothed. It did not. It broke into a series of straight segments. Each segment ended in a jump.\n\nDiscrete force events.\n\nNot wind. Not weather. Not normal refraction.\n\nExternal source inference.\n\nShe wrote it as a sentence, because if she didn’t, the thought would slide away and hide.\n\n**Conclusion:** external forcing function. stepped compression wave moving west→east.\n\nPella leaned over the slate, reading upside down. “Compression wave.”\n\n“Yes.”\n\n“From what.”\n\nTiffani’s mouth went dry. She opened it anyway.\n\n“I don’t know,” she said. A rare sentence. Ugly. Necessary.\n\nPella waited. Pella was good at waiting. It was one of the reasons Tiffani kept her around. Not because she was useful with glass, though she was. Because she did not panic at silence.\n\nTiffani added, quieter, “But it’s not passing over. It’s coming down.”\n\nPella’s eyes widened. “Down where.”\n\nTiffani traced the edge of her projection curve with the pen tip. The curve pointed. The pen didn’t care who lived under it.\n\n“Rim district first,” she said. “Then it tracks toward kiln street if the steps keep spacing the same.”\n\nPella looked out over Saint Merro. The city districts layered under haze and smoke. Rooflines. Furnace chimneys. Anneal houses with their long low roofs. People moving in the streets as dots.\n\n“They don’t know,” Pella said.\n\nTiffani’s jaw clenched. “No.”\n\nPella grabbed the bread packet, shoved it into Tiffani’s free hand. “Eat while you tell someone. Corlis. The platform bell. Anyone with a louder mouth than yours.”\n\nTiffani stared at the bread.\n\nBread was soft. Warm through the cloth. It smelled honest.\n\nHer fingers tried to shake it away. Pride did that. Stubbornness. Stupidity. The whole set.\n\nPella’s hand closed around Tiffani’s wrist. Firm. No room to argue.\n\n“Bread first,” Pella said. “Then you can save the city.”\n\nTiffani’s lips twitched before she could stop it. Not a smile. A leak.\n\n“Do you hear yourself,” she said.\n\nPella’s grin flashed. “I’m extremely inspirational. Eat.”\n\nTiffani tore the bread with her teeth. Too hard. It pulled at her gums. She chewed anyway. The first swallow hurt going down, because her throat had decided it wanted to be tight forever.\n\nShe breathed. Chewed. Swallowed again.\n\nCost worth paying. There’s no bargain.\n\nThe phrase landed in her head uninvited. She hated that it fit. She hated that she needed it. fileciteturn1file4\n\nShe wiped her mouth with the back of her sleeve and reached for the bell cord.\n\nThe grid hum dipped.\n\nThis time it didn’t come back clean.\n\nThe entire platform trembled. Not enough to knock tools. Enough to make the apprentices look up, finally, eyes wide and annoyed, as if the world had interrupted their work on purpose.\n\nA low sound rolled through the iron ribs. Not wind. Not thunder. Pressure.\n\nTiffani’s hand froze on the bell cord.\n\nPella whispered, “That one mattered.”\n\n“Yes,” Tiffani said.\n\nShe yanked the cord.\n\nThe bell’s first strike came out wrong. The metal rang flat. The sound stuttered, then found its tone.\n\nPeople turned in the city below. Too slow. Too scattered. Bell warnings meant different things on different days. Fire. Collapse. Riot. Every crisis used the same damn rope.\n\nTiffani pulled again and again. Three strikes. The platform protocol for “structural event imminent.”\n\nHer own protocol. Written after Marisse. Enforced by guilt and paperwork and the refusal to be surprised again. fileciteturn2file11\n\nThe sky over Seven-Three shifted.\n\nA white line appeared. Thin at first. Clean. Not cloud. Not smoke. A cut in the color.\n\nIt held for two breaths, then widened.\n\nLight changed along its edge. The theodolite lens caught it and split it into multiple bands across the sight glass. Prism behavior without a prism. Refraction under force.\n\nTiffani’s mouth tasted metal. Copper and iron. Particulate in the air already, too fine to see, heavy enough to taste.\n\nPella grabbed her elbow. “We leave. Now.”\n\nTiffani stared at the white line and forced her hands to move. She snapped the lens housing shut. Pulled the spare plate stack into the field kit. Chalk. Cord. Spare slate. The logbook went under her arm.\n\nShe did not leave the page behind.\n\nShe didn’t trust memory. Memory killed people.\n\nAnother tremor hit. Stronger. The bell above them clanged once without her touching it, the vibration throwing the clapper into the metal.\n\nTiffani’s teeth buzzed hard. Pain sharpened along her gums. She tasted blood.\n\nShe got her feet under her.\n\n“Pella,” she said.\n\nPella was already hauling the kit strap over her shoulder. “Yes, Master.”\n\n“We go to the stair run. We stay off the lift. If the grid phase is slipping, I don’t want to be trapped in a box powered by wrongness.”\n\nPella nodded once. No argument. Good apprentice.\n\nTiffani looked back one last time through the theodolite sight, because she couldn’t help herself.\n\nSeven-Three was gone behind the widening line. Not hidden. Replaced.\n\nHer projection curve on the margin pointed directly into the city.\n\nShe closed the logbook.\n\nHard.\n\n“Down,” she said, and meant it as a command to herself.\n\nThey ran for the stairs as the roar began. fileciteturn1file14"

            "## BEAT CATALOG — N01 SCOPE\n\n**Purpose:**  \nDefine all beat methods used in N01 so chapters can be:\n\n- Planned and validated structurally.  \n- Kept unpredictable at the series level.  \n- Emotionally coherent within themselves.\n\nN01 uses **eight** beat methods: BEAT_01 through BEAT_08.\n\n---\n\n### BEAT_01 — Observation → Pattern Recognition\n\n**Function:**  \nUse when the chapter is about **noticing something wrong** and understanding it.\n\n**Structure:**\n\n1. **Baseline Observation**  \n   - POV engages in normal work/routine.  \n   - Small detail feels off (vibration, light behavior, behavior pattern).\n\n2. **Focused Attention**  \n   - POV chooses to pay attention instead of ignoring.  \n   - Compares against prior experience.\n\n3. **Testing / Probing**  \n   - Small actions to test the anomaly.  \n   - Additional observations confirm the anomaly is real.\n\n4. **Pattern Recognition**  \n   - Click moment: “This is not random.”  \n   - POV understands the pattern (or understands that a pattern exists and is dangerous).\n\n5. **Decision / Micro-Shift**  \n   - POV changes course or plan based on the new understanding.\n\n**Emotional Arc:**  \nCuriosity → Unease → Focus → Understanding → Resolve\n\n**Best Used When:**\n- Introducing a core problem.  \n- Showing a character’s core mode of thinking (Jhace sensing structures, Tiffani reading patterns).\n\n**Forbidden Sequences:**\n- Cannot immediately follow another BEAT_01.  \n- Cannot immediately precede BEAT_06 (both are recognition/synthesis-heavy).\n\n**N01 Examples (intended):**\n- Ch 1 (Jhace: “Something Wrong” under the heat-grid).  \n- Ch 2 (Tiffani: observing upper atmosphere anomalies).\n\n---\n\n### BEAT_02 — Trial → Failure → Compounding → Success/Cost\n\n**Function:**  \nUse when you want a **hard failure** that escalates, followed by a victory that hurts.\n\n**Structure:**\n\n1. **Trial Setup**  \n   - Goal is defined (save someone, stabilize structure, train Soulpulse).  \n   - Plan seems plausible but not guaranteed.\n\n2. **Initial Attempt → Failure**  \n   - First attempt fails clearly.  \n   - Stakes increase.\n\n3. **Compounding Problem**  \n   - Failure makes situation worse (more damage, less time, more people at risk).\n\n4. **Reframe / New Approach**  \n   - POV changes approach, often with help from another character.\n\n5. **Success with Explicit Cost**  \n   - Goal is achieved or partially achieved.  \n   - Cost is visible: physical, emotional, moral, or relational.\n\n**Emotional Arc:**  \nHope → Frustration → Panic → Determination → Relief + Dread\n\n**Best Used When:**\n- Training episodes that go wrong.  \n- Major rescue that almost fails.  \n- Moments where price of success must be undeniable.\n\n**Forbidden Sequences:**\n- Cannot follow another BEAT_02.  \n- Should not directly precede BEAT_03 in most cases (risk of fatigue).\n\n**N01 Examples (intended):**\n- Kylar’s first training attempt + follow-up.  \n- A rescue where Jhace’s first plan fails, and Tiffani’s input salvages it.\n\n---\n\n### BEAT_03 — Crisis Front-Loaded → Rolling Complications → Partial Resolution\n\n**Function:**  \nUse for big chaos chapters, especially disasters in progress.\n\n**Structure:**\n\n1. **Drop-In Crisis**  \n   - Chapter opens mid-disaster: building already collapsing, Piercing underway, etc.\n\n2. **Rolling Complications**  \n   - Every attempt to stabilize reveals new problems.  \n   - Stakes grow organically (more people, more structure at risk).\n\n3. **Local Focus Choice**  \n   - POV must choose where to focus attention.  \n   - Implicit acceptance that some things will be left to fail.\n\n4. **Partial Resolution**  \n   - Immediate crisis is stabilized enough to survive.  \n   - Larger structural problem remains unsolved.\n\n5. **Fallout Preview**  \n   - Hints at future consequences for this imperfect solution.\n\n**Emotional Arc:**  \nShock → Scramble → Triage → Exhausted Survival → Uneasy Aftermath\n\n**Best Used When:**\n- Piercing event itself.  \n- Major structural disaster chapters.  \n- Big pivot moments in the novella.\n\n**Forbidden Sequences:**\n- Cannot be used more than 3 times in N01.  \n- Never back-to-back.  \n- Must be buffered by lower-int\nThe file is too long and its contents have been truncated.\n"

Dark hair in short tail. Canvas work clothes, heavy leather tool belt. Moves efficiently, no wasted motion.\n\n### Core Psychology\n\n**Primary Driver: Obsessive Prevention Through Vigilance**\n- Parents died in building collapse when he was 7 Turns (23 people killed total)\n- Investigation concluded \"material fatigue\" – no one caught it in time\n- Has spent 22 Turns trying to be vigilant enough\n- Sees thousands of ways buildings can kill people\n- Cannot unsee potential failures\n\n**The Knot:**\n\"There are thousands of people in this city. I will spend the rest of my life unable to save most of them. I will feel responsible for all of them. This is what it means to have opened my eyes to what I can do.\"\n\n**Isolation as Armor:**\n- Works alone because teaching means inflicting his hypervigilance on others\n- Refuses apprentices (\"That's not a skill, that's anxiety that happens to be useful\")\n- Professional isolation is both choice and inability to connect\n\n### What He Fears\nFailing to prevent a death he could have prevented. Not death itself—*preventable* death. The idea that someone died because he wasn't vigilant enough, wasn't there in time, didn't check the right structure.\n\n### What He Regrets\nEvery person he walked past while responding to another crisis. Every time he chose who to help because he couldn't help everyone. Specific names of people who died while he was saving someone else. The list grows longer.\n\n### What He Lies About\n\"I'm fine.\" He's not. Hasn't been since age 7. The obsessive vigilance is exhausting. The guilt is crushing. But if he admits he's not fine, people might try to make him stop, and stopping means people die.\n\n### What He Pretends to Know\nHow to connect with people normally. He's been so focused on preventing deaths that he's forgotten how to just be with someone without cataloging the ways their environment might kill them. Pretends isolation is practical choice. He meant it genuinely.]\n\n3. **Literalism:** Cannot detect sarcasm. *Someone: \"Great, another crisis, exactly what we needed.\" Jhace: \"We didn't need this. This is bad actually.\"*\n\n4. **The Snort:** When genuinely amused (rare), snort-laughs before he can stop himself. Hates this. Tiffani loves it and deliberately tries to make him snort.\n\n5. **Standing Weird:** When thinking hard, stands in bizarre poses—balanced on one foot, tilted at odd angle, hand on hip like perpetually about to sit but never does. Completely unaware.\n\n### His Actual Laugh\nWhen something is genuinely funny (rare), he CACKLES. Loud, unrestrained, completely unselfconscious. Sharp, almost alarming. Echoes. Copper-gold warmth spreading. The beam needs to hold. light follows stress lines.  \n13) Beam stops settling; evac hands pull Chloen free; cloth tears; breath comes in gasps.  \n14) Jhace holds two more heartbeats to prevent roll; releases.  \n15) **Aftermath cost:** tremor begins in fingers; tries to steady hands by pressing palms to table; tremor persists.  \n3) He attempts a simple forge task (straighten a nail); misses strikes; stops before injury.  \n4) Bram comments once, dry: “Different work today.” No comfort, just direction.  \n5) Tiffani arrives with logbook; she watches Jhace’s hands before she watches his face.  \n6) Jhace tries to reclaim control via testing: hairline crack in a stable wall, no imminent threat.  \n7) **Soulpulse Use #3 fails:** no glow; nothing answers; frustration spikes tremor.  \n8) Tiffani logs the failure condition without blame; she writes “no imminent failure.”  \n9) Runner arrives: kiln corridor brace shifted; people trapped behind a sagging span.  \n10) They move as a unit; Bram supplies wedges and manpower; Pella runs messages.  \n11) Tiffani reads the crack map and marks unsafe standing zones; she pushes crowd back with voice.  \n12) Jhace braces conventionally first: wedges, cord tension, temporary posts; buys time.  \n13) Aftershock begins; conventional brace creeps; crack mouth widens; dust streams down.  \n14) Jhace looks at Tiffani; she nods once; activation becomes justified, not impulsive.  \n15) **Soulpulse Use #4 activation:** contact + protective need; glow enters brace interface and load path.  \n16) Structure holds long enough for evacuation; Tiffani calls release; he releases on first command.  \n17) **Cost:** tremor persists after; vein-lines show briefly during use; exhaustion drops motor control.  \n18) Kylar appears with tremor; tries to hide hands; fails; shame shows as silence.  \n19) Jhace clocks Kylar’s tremor as familiar; fear lands: he is not alone in this.  \n20) Tiffani frames training as safety, not mastery;
